C.2.6
Additional Configurations to Satisfy Requirements
The CSfC (Commercial Solutions for Classified) program outlines security requirements
to ensure robust protection for sensitive data. The following configurations were imple-
mented additional to IPSec VPN Gateway configurations to satisfy additional require-
ments and adhere to the guidelines of the CSfC Multi-Site Connectivity Capability Package
(MSC CP).
• Separation of Networks (MSC-SR-17,MSC-DM-17): Each security domain (Red,
Gray, and Black networks) must be isolated to prevent cross-domain data leakage.
Encryption Components must not perform switching or routing for other Encryption
Components.
! disabling access between Gray and Black Networks except tunnel
Gray1-OEC(config)# access-list 102 deny ip 192.168.1.0 0.0.0.255
192.168.2.0 0.0.0.7
Gray1-OEC(config)# access-list 102 permit ip any any
Gray1-OEC(config)# interface GigabitEthernet1
Gray1-OEC(config-if)# ip access-group 102 in
Gray1-OEC(config-if)# exit
• MSC-SR-19,20: DNS lookup services on network devices must be disabled. Additionally,
DNS server addresses must be specified on solution components, or DNS services must
be disabled.
Gray1-OEC(config)# no ip domain lookup
Gray1-OEC(config)# ip domain name oeccentral.com
• MSC-SR-23: The packet size for packets leaving the external interface of the Gray Firewal-
l/Encryption Component must be configured to prevent fragmentation, considering the MTU
for IPv4 values
Gray1-OEC(config)# crypto ipsec df-bit set
• Dedicated Management Network (MSC-SR-18,MSC-DM-24,28): Management Services
must utilize a dedicated Management Network. Management traffic within the Gray Network
must be secured using encryption protocols such as SSHv2, IPsec, TLS 1.2 or later.
Gray1-OEC(config)# access-list 103 permit tcp 192.168.20.0
0.0.0.255 any eq 22 log
Gray1-OEC(config)# access-list 103 deny tcp any any eq 22 log
Gray1-OEC(config)# access-list 103 deny ip any any
Gray1-OEC(config)# interface GigabitEthernet3
Gray1-OEC(config-if)# ip access-group 103 in
Gray1-OEC(config-if)# exit
Gray1-OEC(config)# line vty 0 4
Gray1-OEC(config-line)# access-class 103 in
Gray1-OEC(config-line)# exit
To validate the security testing, attempt an SSH connection from Site1-Red to Red1-IEC and
another from Red1-WM to Red1-IEC. The connection from Site1-Red will be refused, while
the connection from Red1-WM will succeed. Finally, execute the show logging command
on Red1-IEC to review logs of dropped and permitted SSH connections.

C.3
Implementation Validation and Security Tests
This validation assessed the NSA MSC CP solution’s resilience and compliance with the
CSfC framework. Tests evaluated the effectiveness of dual-layer encryption, VPN con-
figuration accuracy, and access control enforcement in safeguarding classified data as it
traverses untrusted networks. The primary objectives were to ensure data confidentiality,
maintain encryption integrity, validate proper routing through both VPN layers, and con-
firm that unauthorized traffic was neither encrypted nor transmitted. These tests demon-
strate the implementation’s robustness and alignment with CSfC security standards. The
project’s motivation was to provide a feasibility analysis of the NSA MSC CP solution and
test its security resilience before real-world implementation.
Validation Before Tunnel Activation
To ensure that configurations were properly set up but inactive, the following commands
were executed:
• Run show crypto ikev2 sa on the routers to confirm no active IKEv2 sessions.
• Run show crypto ipsec sa to check that the IPsec Security Associations (SAs)
are down but properly configured.
• Run show crypto session detail to confirm the tunnels are inactive with the cor-
rect configuration details displayed.
The results of these validation commands, demonstrating the configured inactive status
of the IKEv2 sessions and IPsec tunnel, are shown in Figure C.5.
Figure C.5: Inactive IKEv2 Sessions and IPsec Tunnel Before VPN Activation
Network Traffic Capture and Tunnel Activation
1. Start Link/Network Capture: Right-click on the links representing the Black and
Gray networks in the simulation environment, select Packet Capturing, and click
Start Capturing.
2. Generate Traffic: Initiate a ping command from the Site1-Red node to the Site2-Red
node (e.g., ping 192.168.22.10 from 192.168.12.10).
3. Verify Tunnel Activation: Execute the following commands on both the Inner En-
cryption Component (IEC) and Outer Encryption Component (OEC) routers:
• Run show crypto ikev2 sa on both IEC and OEC routers to confirm active
IKEv2 sessions, indicating the tunnel was active.

Figure C.6: Validation of IKEv2 Security Associations and IPsec Tunnel Status
• Run show crypto ipsec sa to view active SAs and confirm packet transmis-
sion through the tunnels.
• Run show crypto session detail to display the detailed status of active and
functioning VPN tunnels.
The output of these commands, confirming the activation and proper functioning of
IKEv2 Security Associations and IPsec tunnels, is depicted in Figure C.6.
4. Analyze Captured Packets: Confirm that traffic traversed both tunnels as ESP
packets on packet capture as on Figure C.7. ESP packets are going through this
link, which is an IPSec Tunnel. We cannot see ISAKMP Packets because Cisco
Packet Capture only shows predefined protocols.

Data Transfer Validation
To simulate data transfer across the network, a sample file was created and sent:
1. Create a simple text file on Site1-Red using the following command:
echo "Sample text to test" > file.txt
2. Re-start packet capturing on the links for both the Black and Gray networks.
3. Transfer the file from Site1-Red to Site2-Red using the scp command (Figure C.8):
scp /home/cisco/file.txt cisco@192.168.5.4:/home/cisco
4. Verify that the captured traffic confirms data transmission as ESP packets(Figure
C.9), with no plaintext information exposed. The captured data can be analyzed
further by downloading using tools like Wireshark.
Figure C.8: Steps for file transfer to Site2
Figure C.9: Validation on Site2 has received file
Test Additional Configurations
Validate security measures satisfying CSfC requirements:
• Secure Access to Routers: Access the IEC or OEC routers using the command:
ssh -o KexAlgorithms=+diffie-hellman-group14-sha1 -o HostKeyAlgorithms=+ssh-rsa
cisco@192.168.40.1
156
Analysis, Design and Implementation of a Secure Multi-Site Connectivity Solution
==PAGE:167==
Attempts to SSH from unauthorized nodes should be denied, confirming secure
configurations.
• Restricted Cross-Domain Access: Test cross-domain communication by attempt-
ing to ping:
– From a Black network node to the Gray network.
– From the Gray network to the Red network.
These attempts should fail, verifying the separation of networks and compliance with
CSfC guidelines.
